  • рдЕрдиреНрдпрджрд░реНрд╢рдиреЗ рдХрдердореН ред

  • рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереА рддрд╛рд╡рджреН рдпреБрдХреНрддреИрд╡ ред рдЕрд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджрд╛рд╢реН рдЪреИрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рдЖрддреНрдореИрд╡ “рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░реН рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рджреБрджреЛрд╣” ред рджреЛрд╣рдирдВ рдЪрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирдВ рдкрд░рд╕рдВрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрди ред

  • рдЕрдерд╛рдкрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдореА ред рддрддреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрд╛ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛ рдЖрджрд╛рд╡реН рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрджреЗ, рдЕрддрдГ “рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реН рдЕрдЬрд╛рдпрдд” (рдРрддреНрдмреН рел.рейреи) рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ, рдпрдЬреБрд░реНрд╡реЗрджреЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ “рдЗрд╖реЗ рддреНрд╡реЛрд░реНрдЬреЗ рддреНрд╡рд╛” (рддреНрд╕реН рез.рез.рез) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЗрдбреН рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН, рддрдиреН рдордзреНрдпрд╕реНрдерд╛рдирддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН50 рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдирд╛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рджрд╛рдиреЗрди рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ ред рдКрд░реНрдХреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдГ, рд╕ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд░реН рдПрд╡ ред рдЕрдд рдЖрджрд┐рддреЛ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд╛рджреН рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрд░реН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдкрдорд╛ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛, рдЖрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╡рдореН рдЖрд░реНрддреНрд╡реНрдЬреНрдпрдВ рдмрд╣реБрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рд╢реН рдЪреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╢реН рдЪ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрд░реН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреЗрди рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрди рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрд░реН рдЬрдиреНрдо рдпрдЬреБрд░реНрд╡реЗрджрд╕реНрдп ред рдЕрдирдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕рд╛рдордЧреАрддреНрдпрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдирд┐, рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╢реН рдЪрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рее реирей рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

There are only three deities, Agni, V─Бyu, and Ravi,тАФsay the followers of the Nirukta; even though these three have several names; and in accordance with this theory the text would mean as follows:тАФтАШFor the due fulfilment of the sacrifices,тАЩ to these three deities,тАФthe Dative ending (in the term тАШagniv─Бyuravibhyaс╕етАЩ) being due to the fact of these three deities being the recipients of the sacrificial offerings,тАФтАШhe milked the Brahman,тАЩ called тАШVedaтАЩ, тАШin the forms of с╣Ъk, Yajuс╣г and S─Бman.тАЩ

But as a matter of fact, the root (in тАШdudohaтАЩ тАШmilkedтАЩ) is one that should have two objects; it has its primary object in the form of тАШtrayamтАЩ; and it should have a second, the secondary, object; but there is no such secondary object in the sentence. Hence we conclude that the term тАШravibhyaс╕етАЩ should be taken in the Ablative case; the meaning beingтАФтАШFrom out of the three deities, Agni &c, he extractedтАЩтАФmade to flow, producedтАФ[the Veda].

Question:тАФтАЬHow could the words, the mantra-texts and the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa-texts (of which the Veda consists)тАФwhich are made up of lettersтАФcome out of Agni and other deities?тАЭ Answer:тАФWhy is this not possible? In regard to invisible forces, who can say that they do not exist?

[An objection is raised against the second interpretation preferred by the Bh─Бс╣гya]тАФтАЬIt is not right to alter the meaning of the verb (тАШdundoha,тАЩ тАШmilkedтАЩ); so that (if the root retains its own meaning) how could we havo the Ablative (in тАШagniv─Бyuravibhyaс╕етАЩ)? It should take the Accusative ending, according to the grammatical rule under P─Бс╣ЗiniтАЩs S┼лtra 1.4.51, which lays down that the roots тАШduhi,тАЩ тАШy─БciтАЩ &c., take two objects, and the source from which the тАШmilkingтАЩ is done is the secondary object. Further, the mind of reasonable men is not satisfied when what is described as having happened in the past is something that is not compatible with the ordinary sources of knowledge.тАЭ

This incongruity becomes explained away when we take the statement as referring to the framework of the Vedas; the meaning being that the с╣Ъgveda came out of Agni, the Yajurveda out of V─Бyu and the S─Бmaveda out of Ravi. Then again, it has to be borne in mind that Agni and the rest are deities endowed with superior potencies, and Praj─Бpati is possessed of unexcelled powers; so that what can be impossible for these? Under this explanation full significance should attach to the Ablative; so that the case-relation being already expressed (by the Ablative), and the Ablative being duly significant, it is the Ablative that is used [and not the Accusative, which has been laid down in P─Бс╣Зini 1.4.51 as to be used only in cases where the case-relation is not otherwise expressed]; this has been fully justified in the Bh─Бс╣гya (of Pata├▒jali).

Question:тАФтАЬIf the said theory be not accepted, what would be the explanation of the word тАШagniv─Бyuravibhyaс╕етАЩ then?тАЭ

Answer:тАФIn that case, we have already said that it could be taken as the Dative; and (as regards the necessity of the verb тАШdudoha,тАЩ тАШmilked,тАЩ having a secondary object) it has to be borne in mind that all that is here stated is mere v─Бda. So that (physical impossibilities being not counted) тАШ─БtmanтАЩ may be taken as the required secondary object,тАФthe meaning being that тАШPraj─Бpati milked himself (of the Veda)тАЩ [тАШfor the sake of Agni, and RaviтАЩ]. And further, тАШmilkingтАЩ may be taken in the sense of teaching, which resembles the act of milking in consisting of transferring a thing from one receptacle into another. [So that the passage would mean that тАШhe taught the Veda to Agni &c.тАЩ] Even when the word тАШagniv─Бyuravibhyaс╕етАЩ is taken as Ablative, the statement can be justified on the ground that the opening verses of the с╣Ъgveda speak of Agni,тАФthis fact being what is meant by the statement тАШthe с╣Ъgveda came out of Agni.тАЩ Similarly, the opening verse of the Yajurveda is тАШIс╣гe tvorjeтАЩ &c., whore the term тАШiс╣нтАЩ (the base in тАШiс╣гeтАЩ) means food, and food is produced by V─Бyu, which is present within the food, by the bestowing (upon it) of rain; тАШurkтАЩ (the base in the second word тАШurjeтАЩ) means life-breath, and this is V─Бyu (Air) itself; thus since the Yajurveda opens with the description of the effects of V─Бyu, we have the metaphorical expression that тАШit came out of V─Бyu.тАЩ Or, the duties of the Adhvaryu and the functions of the с╣Ъtviks (which form the subject-matter of the Yajurveda) all consist of so many forms of activity; and all activity proceeds from V─Бyu; hence it is on the basis of this similarity that the Yajurveda is spoken of as coming out of V─Бyu. Lastly, as regards the the singing of the S─Бman cannot be done except by persons specially qualified for it; hence the S─Бma verses are such as can be duly read by only the best among men, and Ravi (the Sun) occupies the highest point in space [and on this fact is based the statement that the S─Бmaveda came out of Ravi ].тАФ(23)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

There are two explanations of this verse, supplied by Medh─Бtithi:тАФ(1) тАШFor the sake of the accomplishment of the sacrifice to Agni, V─Бyu and S┼лrya, He produced the Veda,тАЩ and (2) тАШOut of Agni……He produced the VedaтАЩ;тАФthe latter being preferred, for reasons adduced in the Bh─Бс╣гya.

Burnell has a curious note here to the effect thatтАФтАШThis myth of the creation of the Vedas differs from the S─Бс╣Еkhya account, according to which they are eternal and issue from Brahm─БтАЩs mouth.тАЩ It was necessary to supply references to the work on S─Бс╣Еkhya here referred to.

Medh─Бtithi (p. 19, 1. 9) тАШAsmindar┼ЫaneтАЩтАФetc. This refers to the passage in the Mah─Бhh─Бс╣гya (Nirс╣Зayas─Бgara edition, тАШVol. II, p. 265, l. 18).

A similar use of the Ablative ending we find in 2. 77.

Do. (p. 19, l. 11) тАШDohana├▒ch─Бdhy─БpanamтАЩтАФIn this case ravibhyaс╕е would be the Dative form.

[He created] also Time, the Divisions of Time, the Lunar Mansions, the Planets, the Rivers, the Oceans, the Mountains and the tracts of land, plain and rugged.тАФ(24)

рдзрд░реНрдорд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЖрд╣ ред рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХрд╛рд▓реЛ рд╡реИрд╢реЗрд╖рд┐рдХрд╛рдгрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рд░реВрдкреЛ рд╜рдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдореН ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдЧрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рди рдЖрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдорд╛рдиреН ред рдХрд╛рд▓рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрд╛ рдорд╛рд╕рд░реНрддреНрд╡рдпрдирд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рдирдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдХреГрддреНрддрд┐рдХрд╛рд░реЛрд╣рд┐рдгреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ ред рдЧреНрд░рдГрдЖ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрдпрдГ ред рд╕рд░рд┐рддреЛ рдирджреНрдпрдГ ред рд╕рд╛рдЧрд░рд╛рдГ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ ред рд╢реИрд▓рд╛рдГ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдГ ред рд╕рдорд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрдерд▓рд╛рдиреНрдпреН рдПрдХрд░реВрдкрд╛ рднреВрднрд╛рдЧрд╛рдГ рдЦрд╛рддрдкреНрд░рджрд░рд╡рд░реНрдЬрд┐рддрд╛рдГ ред рд╡рд┐рд╖рдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдЖрд░реЛрд╣рд╛рд╡рд░реЛрд╣рд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рее рез.реирек рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The author mentions Time, because it belongs to the same category (of тАШactionтАЩ) as Duty. It is only according to Vai┼Ыesikas that Time is a substance; according to others it is a form of action; it consists in the extension of the motions of the Sun and other planets, and is liable to return.

тАШDivisious of TimeтАЩтАФsuch divisions as into тАШmonth,тАЩ тАШseason,тАЩ тАШhalf-year,тАЩ тАШyearтАЩ and so forth.

тАШLunar MansionsтАЩтАФsuch as Kс╣Ыttik─Б (Pleiades), Rohiс╣З─л (Aldebaran) and the rest.

тАШPlanetsтАЩтАФSun and the rest.

тАШRiversтАЩтАФstreams.

тАШOceansтАЩтАФseasтАФand тАШMountains.тАЩ

тАШEven tracts of landтАЩтАФsuch tracts of land as are of one uniform form, devoid of ditches and holes.тАФтАШRugged tracts of landтАЩтАФsuch as are high and low.тАФ(24)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Medh─Бtithi (p. 19, 1. 21)тАФIt is interesting to note that even so late as Medh─БtithiтАЩs time, the Lunar Mansions were counted from Kс╣Ыttik─Б onwards, and not from A┼Ыvin─л as in the more recent astronomical systems. (See Thibaut on тАШIndian AstronomyтАЩ in Indian Thought Vol. I.)

This verse is quoted in the Gad─Бdharapaddhati тАФ K─Бlas─Бra, p. 5, as describing the creation of time and its divisions;тАФalso in the K─Бlam─Бdhava (p. 45) as describing the creation of time by God; it reads тАШvibhaktimтАЩ for тАШvibhaktiс╕е.тАЩ

024 Time and the divisions of time, the lunar mansions and the planets, the rivers, the oceans, the mountains, plains, and uneven ground.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдореВрд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Being desirous of bringing into existence these creatures, he created this entire creation (comprising) austerity, speech, happiness, desire and anger.тАФ(25)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рд░рддрд┐рд░реН рдордирд╕рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рддреЛрд╖рдГ ред рдХрд╛рдореЛ рд╜рднрд┐рд▓рд╛рд╖реЛ рдордиреНрдордереЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреН рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН ред рдПрд╡рдорд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛рдВ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдВ рд╕рд╕рд░реНрдЬреЗрдорд╛рдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЪ рдпрд╛ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд░реН рдЙрдХреНрддрд╛ ред рдЗрдорд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд░рд╖реНрдЯреБрдореН рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕реБрд░рд╛ рдпрдХреНрд╖рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдЧрдиреНрдзрд░реНрд╡рд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реН рддрджреБрдкрдХрд░рдгрдВ рддрджрд╛рддреНрдордзрд░реНрдорд╡рдЪреН рдЫрд░реАрд░рдВ рдзрд░реНрдордВ рдЪрд╛рджрд╛рд╡реН рдЕрд╕реГрдЬрджреН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрде рдХреЗрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪреЛрдпреБрдХреНрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдВ рд╕рд╕рд░реНрдЬреЗрддрд┐ ред рдп рдПрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдВ рдХреГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдзрд╛рддрд╡рдГ рдХрд░реЛрддреНрдпрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рд╡рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рдиреНрдиреЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдкрдЪрддрд┐ рдкрд╛рдХрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐, рдпрдЬрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рдЧрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдХреГрджрдиреНрддрд╛рджреН рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗ рд╜рд╡рдЧрдд рдЖрдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрдЧрддреЛ рдзрд╛рддреБрдГ рдХрд░реЛрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердорд╛рддреНрд░рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдирдкрд░реЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдиреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдХреБрддрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрдиреНрдиреЗ рдкреБрдирдГрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдиреЗ рд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрджреЛрд╖реЛ рдорд╛ рднреВрджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рд░рдХрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рддрд╛рддреНрдкрд░реНрдпрдореН ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рд╕реГрдЬреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛ рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрд╛рд╡рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рдиреНрдирд╛ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯреЗрдГ рдХрд░реНрдо, рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рдкреЛрд╖рдВ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдЗрддрд┐ рее реирел рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШHappinessтАЩтАФSatisfaction of the mind тАШDesireтАЩтАФLonging or Love; the rest are well known.

тАШHe created this creationтАЩ comprising the things mentioned and others of the same kind.тАФThe term тАШthisтАЩ refers to the creation of things mentioned in this verse as also that described in the foregoing verses.

тАШBeing desirous of bringing into existence these creaturesтАЩтАФsuch, for instance, as the Devas and Asuras, the Yakс╣гa, the R─Бkс╣гasa, and Gandharva and other beings, the vehicle of these beings, in the form of the body equipped with the soul and characteristics, and also Dharma; these he created first of all.

тАЬWhat sort of verbal expression is thisтАФтАШhe created the creationтАЩ?тАЭ It means exactly what is meant by the expression тАШhe wrought or did the creationтАЩ; as a matter of fact, all verbal roots express some particular form of action, denoted by the root тАШKс╣ЫтАЩ; e.g., тАШcooksтАЩ is synonymous with тАШdoes the cooking; тАШsacrificesтАЩ is the same as тАШdoes the sacrificingтАЩ; in the expression under question the peculiar form of the action (of creation) having been already expressed by the verbal noun (тАШcreationтАЩ), the root contained in the verb (тАШcreatedтАЩ) comes to denote only the action. To guard against such an expression living open to the charge of being a needless repetition, involved in the action being spoken of by means of the root in the verb, after it has been already expressed by the verbal noun,тАФwe may take the mention of the verb to be for the purpose of expressing the tense and the voice (which could not be expressed by the verbal noun).тАФOr, the term тАШcreationтАЩ may be taken as standing for the particular created things known by the ordinary means of knowledge and forming the object of the general act of creating expressed by the verb тАШcreatedтАЩ; such usage being analogous to the expression тАШsvapoс╣гam puс╣гс╣нaс╕е,тАЩ тАШreared the rearing by oneselfтАЩ (where the rearing qualified by тАШselfтАЩ forms the object of the verb тАШrearedтАЩ, which denotes rearing in general).тАФ(25)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдзрд░реНрдореМ рд╡реНрдпрд╡реЗрдЪрдпрддреН рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдХреЗрди рдкреГрдердЧреНрднрд╛рд╡реЗрди рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН- “рдЕрдпрдВ рдзрд░реНрдо рдПрд╡, рдЕрдпрдореН рдЕрдзрд░реНрдо рдПрд╡” ред

  • рдирдиреБ рдЪ рдиреИрд╡рд╛рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдХреЛ рд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╣рд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдпреН рдЙрднрдпрд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдордХрд╛рдирд┐ ред рдпрдерд╛рд╣реБрдГ- “рд╢рдмрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рд╡реИрджрд┐рдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐, рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рд╕рд╛рдзрдирдХрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ред рдпрдерд╛ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛрдордГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкреЗрдг рдзрд░реНрдореЛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдЩреНрдЧрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рддреНрд╡реН рдЕрдзрд░реНрдордГ” рдЗрддрд┐ ред

  • рдЕрдд рдЖрд╣ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рддреБ рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдХрд╛рдп ред рдХрд░реНрдорд╢рдмреНрджреЗрдирд╛рддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░реЛрдпреЛрдЧрдГ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдореН рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирдореН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕ рдПрд╡ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рд╜рдиреНрдпрдерд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпреБрдЬреНрдпрдорд╛рдиреЛ рд╡рд┐рдкрд░реАрддрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡реЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдзрд░реНрдордГ рд╕рдиреНрдиреН рдЕрдзрд░реНрдорд░реВрдкрддрд╛рдореН рдЖрдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ, рдЕрдзрд░реНрдореЛ рдзрд░реНрдорддреНрд╡рдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реИрд╡ ред рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛ рдмрд╣рд┐рдГрдкреНрд░рдпреБрдЬреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдЕрдзрд░реНрдордГ рд╕рдГ, “рди рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐” рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдЧреЛрдЪрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ред рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрд╡реЗрджрд┐рдХреГрддрд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдореАрдпреЗ рдзрд░реНрдордГ, рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ред рдПрд╡рдВ рддрдкреЛ51 рдзрд░реНрдордГ, рддрджреН рдПрд╡ рддреБ рджрдореНрднреЗрдирд╛рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛52 рд╡рд╛ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрдореН рдЕрдзрд░реНрдордГ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд░рдЧрдордирдВ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдгрд╛рдореН рдЕрдзрд░реНрдордГ, рдЧреБрд░реБрдирд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдиреАрдирд╛рдВ рдШреГрддрд╛рдХреНрддрд╛рджреНрдпрдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣реЗрдг рдзрд░реНрдордГ ред рдЕрддрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкреИрдХрддреНрд╡реЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрднреЗрджрд╛рджреН рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдзрд░реНрдорд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛ ред рдПрдХрддреНрд╡реЗ рд╜рдкрд┐53 рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рджреГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛54 рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрднреЗрдж рдПрд╡ ред

  • рдЕрде рдЪ рдХрд░реНрдордлрд▓реЗрд╖реБ рдХрд░реНрдорд╢рдмреНрджрдГ, рдХрд╛рд░рдгреЗ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреЛрдкрдЪрд╛рд░рд╛рддреН55 ред рддреЗрдиреИрддрджреН рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐- рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╡реЗрдЪрдпрддреН рдХрд░реНрдордлрд▓рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрд╛рдп ред рдХрдГ рдкреБрдирдГ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рдлрд▓рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрдГ ред рдЕрдд рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН- рджреНрд╡рдиреНрджреНрд╡реИрд░реН рдЕрдпреЛрдЬрдпрддреН рд╕реБрдЦрджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ ред рдзрд░реНрдорд╕реНрдп рдлрд▓рдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдореН рдЕрдзрд░реНрдорд╕реНрдп рджреБрдГрдЦрдореН ред рдЕрдд рдЙрднрдпрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреЛ рджреНрд╡рдиреНрджреНрд╡реИрд░реН рдпреЛрдЬреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ, рдзрд░реНрдордХрд╛рд░рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╕реБрдЦреЗрди, рдЕрдзрд░реНрдордХрд╛рд░рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рджреБрдГрдЦреЗрди ред рджреНрд╡рдиреНрджреНрд╡рд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рд╜рдпрдВ рд░реВрдвреНрдпрд╛ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╡рд┐рд░реБрджреНрдзреЗрд╖реБ рдкреАрдбрд╛рдХрд░реЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рд╢реАрддреЛрд╖реНрдгрд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛рддрдкрдХреНрд╖реБрддреНрд╕реМрд╣рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ ред рдЖрджрд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рднрд╛рд╡реЗрди рдЬреНрдЮреЗрдпрдореН ред рдХреЗрд╡рд▓реМ рд╕реБрдЦрджреБрдГрдЦрд╢рдмреНрджреМ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрдирд░рдХрдпреЛрд░реН рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХреМ рдирд┐рд░рддрд┐рд╢рдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдкрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдкрд╡рдЪрдиреМ рд╡рд╛ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ56 рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордкреБрддреНрд░рдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд▓рд╛рднрд╕реН рддрджрдкрд╣рд╛рд░рд╢реН рдЪрд╛рджрд┐рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ ред рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдореН рдЙрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдЙрдХреНрддрд╛ ред рдЕрдиреЗрди рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореН рдПрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрдГ рдлрд▓рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрд╢реН рдЪ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдирд╛ рдХреГрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджреНрдпрд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдХрдГ рее рез.реирем рее

M G: vi┼Ыeс╣гa

D (5: 601) suggests: k─Бrye k─Бraс╣Зopac─Бr─Бt

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШHe differentiated Virtue and ViceтАЩтАФHe fixed their character by due distinction, i.e., as distinct from each other; in such formтАФтАШthis is Virtue, that is Vice.тАЩ

Objection:тАФтАЬIn reality however, there is no such hard and fast distinction; there are several actions that partake of the nature of both and are both virtuous and vicious (sinful); for instance, they say that the actions (of sacrifice) laid down in the Veda are of mixed character, being accomplished, as they are, by means of animal-slaughter; the sacrifice for instance, is by itself a virtuous or meritorious act, but by reason of animal-slaughter forming one of its factors, it is vicious or sinful.тАЭ

It is in view of this objection that the text has added the phraseтАФтАШFor the due discrimination of actionsтАЩ;тАФthe term тАШactionтАЩ here stands for the actual process, the performance of actions; as a matter of fact, the same act, if performed in a different manner, acquires an entirely different character; i.e., an act which is virtuous (when done in one way) becomes vicious (when done in another way), and vice vers├в; e.g. the act of animal-slaughter itself; animal-slaughter, when done apart from a sacrificial performance, is vicious, sinful,тАФforming as it does the subject of such Vedic prohibitions as тАШOne should not kill any animalsтАЩ; but when done within the sacrificial altar, during the Agn─лс╣гom─лya offering, it in virtous, meritoriousтАФbeing an act that forms the subject of injunctions. Similarly, Austerity (in itself) is virtuous; but when it is performed through hypocrisy, or by a person unfit for performing it, it is vicious. Similarly again, for women, intercourse with the husbandтАЩs younger brother is sinful; but when under orders from her elders, a woman desiring children has intercourse with her brother-in-law, who is besmeared with clarified butter &c. (as laid down in the scriptures), it is virtuous. Thus then, even though the action be one and the same, there is a distinction based upon the way in which it is actually performed. The sameness of the action however is only apparent; in view of other sources of knowledge the acts (done in different ways) are different.

Further, the term тАШactionтАЩ may be taken as standing for the effects of the actions,тАФthe cause being figuratively spoken of as the effect. Thus the meaning comes to be as follows:тАФтАШHe differentiated actions for the due discrimination of the effects of actions.тАЩ

In view of the question as to what is the тАШdiscrimination of the effects of actions,тАЩ it is addedтАФтАШhe connected them with pairs of opposites, in the shape of Plensure-Pain and the likeтАЩ;тАФтАШPleasureтАЩ being the effect of тАШVirtueтАЩ and тАШPainтАЩ of тАШVice.тАЩ It is thus that people performing both kind of actions become associated with these pairs of opposites; by performing virtuous acts they become associated with pleasure, and by performing vicious acts they become connected with pain.

The term тАШdvanс╕НvaтАЩ, тАШPair of opposites,тАЩ is, by usage, applied to such mutually contradictory sources of pain as тАШHeat-Cold,тАЩ тАШRain-Hot weather,тАЩ тАШHunger-Satiation,тАЩ and so forth.

The phrase тАШand the likeтАЩ refers to the general and special forms of the said sources of pain. For instance, the terms тАШPleasure-Pain,тАЩ in their general form are denotative either of тАШHeaven-Hell,тАЩ or of тАШexcessive joy and sorrowтАЩ; while in their special form, they stand for the тАШobtaining of heaven, of landed property, of sons, of cattle and so forth (тАШPleasureтАЩ) and the тАШbeing deprived of theseтАЩ; all these being implied by the terms тАШ─Аdi,тАЩ тАШand the like.тАЩ

The creation of Actions having been described before (in Verse 18 et seq.), what is described in the present verse is that Praj─Бpati brought about the distinction in their actual performance, as also the discrimination of their effects; thus there is a difference between what was said before and what is said now.тАФ(26)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

The term тАШdharmaтАЩ, as Burnell rightly remarks, stands for a manтАЩs whole duty, including both secular and religious duty.тАЩ

The other тАШDvandvasтАЩ are K─Бma (Desire)тАФKrodha (Anger)тАФR─Бga (Attachment)тАФDveс╣гa (Hatred)тАФтАШKс╣гut (Hunger) тАФPip─Бs─Б (Thirst)тАФHarс╣гa (joy)тАФViс╣г─Бda (Sorrow)тАЩ and so forth.

026 Moreover, in order to distinguish actions, he separated merit from demerit, and he caused the creatures to be affected by the pairs (of opposites), such as pain and pleasure.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдореВрд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The evanescent subtile constituents of the half-ten (Elemental Substances) that have been described,тАФalong with those, this whole (world) comes forth, in due order.тАФ(27)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдЙрдкрд╕рдВрд╣рд╛рд░реЛ рд╜рдпрдореН ред рджрд╢рд╛рд░реНрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдорд╣рд╛рднреВрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрд╛ рдЕрдгреНрд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдорд╛ рдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛ рдЕрд╡рдпрд╡рд╛рд╕реН рддрдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реН рддрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рд┐рдиреНрдпрдГ ред рдкрд░рд┐рдгрд╛рдордзрд░реНрдорд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╕реНрдереМрд▓реНрдпрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рд┐рдиреНрдп рдЙрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╛рд░реНрдзрдореН рдЗрджрдВ рдЬрдЧрддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рддреНрдпреН рдЙрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдиреБрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╢рдГ рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг ред рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдорд╛рддреН рд╕реНрдереВрд▓рдВ рд╕реНрдереВрд▓рд╛рддреН рд╕реНрдереВрд▓рддрд░рдореН ред рдпрд╛рджреГрд╢реЛ рд╡рд╛ рдХреНрд░рдо рдЙрдХреНрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдХреН рее рез.реирен рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

This verse sums up what has gone before.

тАШOf the half-tenтАЩтАФi.e., of the five elemental substances;тАФтАШthe subtile,тАЩтАФminute,тАФтАШconstituents,тАЩтАФparts; i.e., the тАШRudimentary substancesтАЩ; these are тАШevanescentтАЩ;тАФthey are called тАШevanescentтАЩ (liable to destruction) in the sense that, being liable to undergo modifications, they take up grosser forms.тАФтАШalong with those,’ тАШthis wholeтАЩтАФworld,тАФтАШcomes forth,тАЩтАФis produced;тАФтАШin due order,тАЩтАФin proper sequence; i.e., from the subtile the gross, and from the gross the grosser; or in the order in which they have been described (in the foregoing verses).тАФ(27)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШVin─Б┼Ыinyaс╕етАЩтАФbecause liable to change into gross substances (Medh─Бtithi, Govinda and Kull┼лka); or because they are products (R─Бghav─Б.)

The commentators are at some pains to explain the incongruity of the inter-position of the present verse in the middle of what purports to be a connected account of the process of creation. Medh─Бtithi says the verse serves the purpose of summing up what has been said so far;тАФGovindar─Бja and Kull┼лka make it serve the purpose of setting aside the notion that the creation was accomplished by Brahman without the help of the тАШprinciplesтАЩ;тАФand N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa holds that it is meant to lay stress upon the non-eternality of atoms;тАФNandana has solved the difficulty by placing this verse after verse 19.

B├╝hler

027 But with the minute perishable particles of the five (elements) which have been mentioned, this whole (world) is framed in due order.

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрджреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░реН рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЛ рднреВрддрд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯреМ рд╢рдХреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ рдпрдереЗрдЪреНрдЫрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирдГ рд╕реНрд░рд╖реНрдЯреБрдВ рддрдерд╛рдкрд┐ рди рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХрд▓реНрдкрдХреГрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдпреН рдЕрдирдкреЗрдХреНрд╖реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирдГ рд╕реГрдЬрддрд┐ ред рдпреЗрди рдпрд╛рджреГрд╢рдВ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдХрд▓реНрдкреЗ рдХрд░реНрдо рдХреГрддрдВ рддрддреНрдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрддрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рддреМ рддрдВ рдЬрдирдпрддрд┐, рди рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░реЗ ред рд╢реБрднреЗрди рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рддрддреНрдлрд▓реЛрдкрднреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдЬрд╛рддреМ рдЬрдирдпрддрд┐, рд╡рд┐рдкрд░реАрддреЗрди рддрд┐рд░реНрдпрдХреНрдкреНрд░реЗрддрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ ред рдпрдереИрд╡ рднреВрддреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрдЧреБрдгрд╛рдГ рдХрд▓реНрдкрд╛рджреМ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд╕реНрдерд╛ рдЙрджреНрднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдПрд╡рдВ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд▓рдпреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд┐ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЙрджреНрднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╛рджреМ ред “рддрддрдГ рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг” рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрд╖ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╕реН рддрддреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдЕрд╕реНрддреНрдпреН рдПрд╡ ред

  • рдпрджрд┐ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖реЛрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐рдГ, рдХреНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддреЗрд░реН рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдореН рдЙрдкрдпреЛрдЧрд┐ рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдореН рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдореН ред рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕рддрд┐ рдЬрдЧрдд рдЙрддреНрдкрддреНрддреЗрдГ, рдХрдердореН рдЕрдиреБрдкрдпреЛрдЧрдГ ред рди рддрдореН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реЗрдг рд╕реНрдерд┐рддреНрдпреБрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд▓рдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдирд┐рддреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рдХреГрддрд╛рдиреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рддрджрд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рдкрд░рд┐рдгрд╛рдорд╢реН рдЪ ред рдПрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╕рд╛рдордЧреНрд░реНрдпрд╛ рдЗрджрдВ рдЬрдЧрджреН рдЙрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд▓реАрдпрддреЗ рдЪ ред рд╕рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдВ рди рд╡рд┐рд╣рдиреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрдереЗрд╣ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рджрд┐рд░реН рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЛ рднреГрддреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдиреН рдлрд▓реЗрди рдпреЛрдЬрдпреЗрджреН рдПрд╡рдореН рдПрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдиреБрд░реВрдкреЗрдгреИрд╡ рдпреЛрдЬрдпрддрд┐ ред рди рдЪрд╛рдиреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ ред

  • рдирдиреБ рдирд╛рд╕реНрдп рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрде рдкреНрд░рддреАрдпрддреЗ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдпрддреЗ ред рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рддреБрд░реН рдПрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрдорд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рддрдиреНрддреНрд░реНрдпрдореН ред рд╕ рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╛рджреМ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рддреНрдордХреЗ рддрджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрд░реАрддреЗ рд╡рд╛ рдиреНрдпрдпреБрдЩреНрдХреНрдд рд╕ рддрджреН рдПрд╡ рдХрд░реНрдо рднрдЬрддреЗ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ ред рди рдкрд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рджреЗрд░реН рдЕрдиреБрд╢рд╛рд╕рдирдореН рдЕрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡реЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛рдиреНрдпрдерд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐, рдкреНрд░рд╛рдХреНрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрд╡рд╢рд╛рддреН рд╕рд╛рдзреНрд╡реН рдЕрд╕рд╛рдзреБ рд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╢рд╛рд╕рдирдирд┐рд░рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖реЛ рд╜рдиреБрддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ ред рд╕реГрдЬреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рд╣реН рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЬрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирдГ ред рдХрд▓реНрдкрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗ рд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдиреН рдПрд╡ рд╡рд╛ рдХрд▓реНрдкреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░реН рдПрд╡ рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдВрд╢реН рддрддреНрдХрд░реНрддреГрддреНрд╡реЗрди рдирд┐рдпреБрдЩреНрдХреНрддреЗ ред рдЕрддрд╕реН рддрдиреНрдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдореН рдПрд╡рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЪреАрдирдВ рд╢реБрднрдореН рдЕрд╢реБрднрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реНрдо рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрджреН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН ред

  • рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рддреБ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЪрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ ред рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдкрдиреНрдирд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреНрдордиреЛ рди рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЬрд╛рддрд┐рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд╛ ред рдЕрддрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреБрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдГ ред рдпрдВ рдЬрд╛рддрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдВ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдирд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкрд░рд╡рдзрд╛рджреМ рд╕ рд╕рд┐рдВрд╣рд╛рджрд┐рдЬрд╛рддреАрдп рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рд╕рдВрдкрдиреНрдиреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрддреНрд╡реЗ рдорд╛рд░реНрджрд╡рдореН рдЕрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╣рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЬрд╛рддрд┐рдзрд░реНрдордВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрдирд╛рдиреБрдкрджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ ред рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдХреГрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧрднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдВ рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рдЧрддрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрдорд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рд┐рддрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее рез.реирео рее

рдПрддрджреН рдПрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The meaning of this verse is as follows:тАФEven though Praj─Бpati, being the supreme director of the creation of things, can create living creatures just as he chooses, yet, as a matter of fact, he creates them, not without reference to the actions done by them during the preceding cycles; he makes the creature born in that family of creatures which is indicated by the act done by it during the previous cycle,тАФand never in any other family; if the creature has, in the past, done a good act, it is led to be born in a family in which it would be enabled to experience the good results of that act,тАФin such families for instance, as тАШGod,тАЩ тАШManтАЩ and so forth; if, on the other hand, the acts of the creature have been bad, it is born in such families as тАШanimals,тАЩ тАШevil spiritsтАЩ and the like. What happens is that at the beginning of each new creation, the acts done by creatures in the previous cycle come out, after having, during Dissolution, lain latent within their source; just in the same manner as the Elements, the Organs and the Constituent Attributes come out at the beginning of each creation, after having lain latent within their source, in the Boot Evolvent. And the reason for this lies in the fact that the law relating to the тАШresidue of the pastтАЩ (affecting the future) applies with equal force to the case in question also.

Question:тАФтАЬIf the coming into existence (of a creature) is dependent upon its own past acts, where then does the almighty power of Praj─Бpati come in? Of what sort too would be the almighty power which is dependent upon extraneous influences?тАЭ

Answer:тАФIt is only when the said almighty power is there and (active) that the world comes into existence; how then can the said power he said to have no effect at all? In fact, neither continuance, nor production, nor dissolution (of the world) is possible except when that power is present,тАФthe power of God being ever present, at all times. In reality, what lead to a creature being born are (1) acts done by itself, (2) the will of Praj─Бpati and (3) the evolution of the Root Evolvent. It is by all this set of causes that this world is produced, exists and becomes dissolved. The mere fact of Praj─Бpati being influenced by the things does not deprive him of his almighty power. The case stands upon the same footing as a king bestowing upon his servants and dependents the rewards for acts done by them; exactly in the same manner Praj─Бpati assigns to each creature what is in accordance with its previous acts; and yet neither the King nor Praj─Бpati cease to be тАШall-powerful.тАЩ

Objection:тАФ

тАЬThe meaning assigned to the verse does not appear to be its right meaning at all. What appears to be its right meaning is that the Creator is entirely independent in assigning their work to the creatures. The verse thus means as follows:тАФтАШEvery creature conformed to,тАФi.e., carried onтАФthat same actionтАФin the form either of doing harm to others, or its contrary,тАФto which the Lord had directed it atтАФat the beginning of creationтАЩ; that is, man does not have recourse to actions, cither entirely on the advice of his father and other elders, or by his own will; in fact, whatever good or bad action he performs, he does wholly in accordance with Praj─БpatiтАЩs directions, entirely uninfluenced by the advice of any other person.

тАШWhen created againтАЩтАФi.e., when born again, whether in another cycle, or in this same cycle,тАФit is Praj─Бpati alone who directs all animate beings to be the doers of actions; hence even past good and bad acts arc done by them only in obedience to the directions of Praj─Бpati; this has been thus declared:тАФтАШThey become agents without being masters of their own actions; to the good or the bad act they are led on by GodтАЩ; and again тАШthis ignorant creature has no control over his pleasure and pain; it is only as led on by God that he goes to heaven or to hell.тАЩтАЭ

To the above we make the following reply:тАФIf the suggested explanation were accepted, (1) it would mean the abandoning of the idea of an inseparable connection between Actions and their results,тАФ(2) it would also mean that all human effort is useless (everything being determined entirely by the independent will of God),тАФ(3) and it would mean that the injunctions of the Agnihotra and such acts, as well as the worshipping of Brahman, are entirely futile; in fact it would come to this that actions for visible or invisible results would be undertaken by only such men as are ignorant of the nature of God; while those who are of opinion that the doing of actions and the enjoying of their results are dependent on the will of God would never engage in any form of activity; they would keep away from activity under the impression that тАШeven though an action may be done, its result may not follow (if God so wished it), and even though we may not do the act, we may enjoy its results (if God so willed it).тАЩ Especially because the desire for being the doer of a certain act does not arise in the man forcibly through the prompting of God, as illness arises from unwholesome food; on the other hand, if the said desire is held to be determined by the connection between the action and its result,тАФthe idea being that тАШthis result follows from this actionтАЩтАФthen it would not be true that тАШthe Lord directed the man to the actтАЩ (as the text says).

The direction by God, spoken of in the text can be admitted only on the authority of the scriptures; and in the statementтАФтАШthat action to which the Lord directed him at first,тАЩтАФthe phrase тАШat firstтАЩ is used in reference to the present, since the world is beginningless (so that тАШat firstтАЩ could not mean at the beginning of creation)тАЩ, and as regards the тАШdirectionтАЩ or тАШsupervisionтАЩ by the Lord, this extends over all tilings (not only to Actions), he being the efficient cause of Time and Space (within which all things have their being). [In this way the idea of GodтАЩs supervision is not incompatible with the theory that results accrue to men from their own acts.]

Other people offer the following explanation of the verse:тАФWhen a personality happens to be born in a different animal-species (from that in which it was born in its former life), it does not require the effects of its former conditions; nor is there the resultant continuity of its former nature; when, for instance, a certain personality happens to be born in the foline species, which species God originally prompted to such acts as the killing of others and the like,тАФit renounces the quality of mercy which it may have practised during its human existence, and acquires the quality of that species in which it is born, even though this latter quality may not have been taught by any one. What is meant is that the actions due to the nature of the personality being ordained by God are extremely potent, and make the personality forget its former habits.

The idea contained in this verse is further expanded in the following verse.тАФ(28)

B├╝hler

028 But to whatever course of action the Lord at first appointed each (kind of beings), that alone it has spontaneously adopted in each succeeding creation.

Each being, when created again and again, naturally conformed to that same act to which the lord had, at first, directed him.тАФ(28)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

(verse xviii)

Medh─Бtithi notes two explanations of this verse.

The natural meaning appealтАЩs to be that тАШeach being continues, in each succeeding Birth, to betake itself to the same function that was assigned to it in the beginning by Praj─Бpati.тАЩ

But this being incompatible with the law of Karma, which has been regarded as adumbrated by Manu in I. 41,тАФMedh─Бtithi has tried his best to get out of the words the meaning that the conditions and activities of each being are ordained in accordance with his past deeds;тАФbut the only argument that he puts forward in support of assigning this meaning is that the literal meaning of the words would give rise to a number of undesirable contingencies. According to Medh─Бtithi, creation is due to the joint action of the three causesтАФ(1) the beingтАЩs past acts (2) GodтАЩs will and (3) Evolution of Prakс╣Ыti.

The confusion of thought in regard to the exact meaning of this and the following two verses is further shown by the fact that Medh─Бtithi (p. 22, l, 27 under verse 30) has thought it necessary to set forth тАШanother explanationтАЩ of these texts.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

(verse xviii-xix)

Mah─Бbh─Бrata, 12.232.16.тАФтАШOf the created things, whatever functions became assigned to whichever thing at the beginning of creation, that thing take to those same functions, whenever they are created again and again.тАЩ тАШHarmfulness or harmlessness, gentleness or ferociousness, righteousness or unrighteousness, truthfulness or untruthfulness, with one or the other of these they are obsessed, and hence are they fond of just those.тАЩ

029 Whatever he assigned to each at the (first) creation, noxiousness or harmlessness, gentleness or ferocity, virtue or sin, truth or falsehood, that clung (afterwards) spontaneously to it.

Just as on the approach of the turn of the Seasons, each season, by itself, acquires its own seasonal characteristics,тАФso in the same manner living beings take up their respective lines of action.тАФ(30)

  • (рез.рейреж) рдЕрд╡реНрдпрднрд┐рдЪрд░рд┐рддрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреАрдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ ред рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдпрдерд░реНрддреБрд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдиреАрддрд┐ ред рд╢реЗрд╖рдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдореН рее рез.рейреж рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

In support of what has been said in the foregoing verses, an illustration is cited. Just as even inanimate things have their character fixed by the law of God,тАФso animate beings also do not go beyond the law laid down by Praj─Бpati, in accordance with the past acts of men; they have recourse to that same line of action which has been assigned to the family of beings in which they are born; any other line of action they cannot take up, even though they may wish to do so.

тАШThe seasonsтАЩтАФSpring and the rest;тАФтАШits own seasonal characteristicsтАЩтАФin the form of leaves, flowers, cold, heat, rain and so forth.тАФтАШat the approach of the turnтАЩтАФwhen the turn, the occasion for functioning, of a particular season arrives,тАФthat season acquires its character, by itself; and it does not stand is need of any act of man. For instance, at the advent of spring, mango-blossoms bloom forth by themselves, and they, do not stand in need of watering at the roots. In the same manner the тАШlines of actionтАЩ of menтАФwhich exist in their тАШunseenтАЩ or latent formтАФ[operate by themselves]. As a matter of fact, there is no such thing as is not affected by the тАШactsтАЩ (of men); for instance, it is in the nature of the Rainy Season that there should be rain, and yet on account of the faulty action, either of the king or kingdom itself, there is sometimes drought. From all this it follows that the force of тАШactionтАЩ is irrepressible.

The frequent repetition of the term тАШс╣ЫtuтАЩ season,тАЩ is due to the exigencies of metre.

B├╝hler

030 As at the change of the seasons each season of its own accord assumes its distinctive marks, even so corporeal beings (resume in new births) their (appointed) course of action.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШWith a view to the development of the regions.тАЩ terrestrial and the rest;тАФтАШdevelopmentтАЩ stands for Nourishment and expansion; it is only when the four castes, Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and the rest, are there that there is development of the three regions; for the Gods live upon offerings made by these castes,тАФthese castes alone being entitled to the performance of sacrifices; so that the action done by these nourishes the two regions (celestial and subterranean); then again, the Gods also are prompted by menтАЩs action to act; from the Sun-God comes rain; and thus the said creation (of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa) tends to the nourishment of this (terrestrial) region also.

тАШHe brought unto existence,тАЩтАФi.e., produced, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and other castes,тАФтАШfrom out of his mouth, armтАЩ, thighs and feetтАЩ respectively; i.e., the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa from out of his mouth, the Kс╣гatriya out of his arms, the Vai┼Ыya out of his thighs and the ┼Ъ┼лdra out of his feet.тАФThe affix тАШtasiтАЩ (in тАШmukha b─Бh─Бrup─Бdataс╕етАЩ) has the sense of the Ablative; the effect is, as it were, drawn out of the cause; and this implying a sort of separation, the use of the Ablative becomes fully justified.

It was only a certain primeval Br─Бhmaс╣Зa whom Praj─Бpati produced, by his divine power, out of the component particles of his own mouth; because so far as the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas of the present day are concerned, they are all actually found to he produced by intercourse between human couples, out of the material principles.

In reality however, what is stated here is merely commendatory, intended to show the relative superiority and inferiority of the castes;тАФthe meaning beingтАФтАШof all beings Praj─Бpati is the highest,тАФamong all the limbs of Praj─Бpati, the mouth is the highest,тАФsimilarly the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is the highest, most praiseworthy, of all the castes;тАЩ and on the basis of this similarity the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is described as produced out of BrahmaтАЩs mouth.

Or, the description of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa coming out of BrahmaтАЩs mouth may be due to the fact that the work of the mouth, such as teaching and the like, belongs preeminently to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa; to the Kс╣гatriya belongs the work of the arms, lighting; to the Vai┼Ыya the work of the thighs, such as wandering about with the cows, when tending cattle, and also travelling for trade on land and water; and to the ┼Ъ┼лdra belongs the work of the feet, i.e., service.тАФ(31)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШLokavivс╣ЫddhyarthamтАЩтАФтАШin order that the inhabitants of the worlds might multiply (or prosper)тАЩтАФ(Medh─Бtithi, Govindar─Бja and Kull┼лka);тАФтАШin order to protect the world by means of the castes, and to make it prosperousтАЩ (N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa).

It is refreshing to find Medh─Бtithi regarding this account of the castes issuing from the mouth and other parts of the body of the Lord as mere тАШstutiтАЩтАФnot to be taken as literally true.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The creation described here is apparently of another Being; but others have held that it is of the same Brahm─Б; the meaning being that the body that came out of the Egg being divided into two halves, тАШwith one half he became MaleтАЩтАФi.e., he became a male being, capable of instilling semenтАФand тАШwith the other half he became the FemaleтАЩ; that is, his body assumed the form of the Hermaphrodite, like Gaur─л-┼Ъaс╣Еkara (combined in a single body). Or, it may mean that he crested the Female apart (from the Male).тАФHaving created her, he produced, from her, by the act of procreation, that being whose well-known name is тАШVir─Бj.тАЩ What is meant is that Praj─Бpati had recourse to his own daughter.

This mention of the bifurcation of Praj─БpatiтАЩs body is based upon the fact that the husband and wife differ only in their bodies, and in all functions they are entirely united.тАФ(32)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

That Medh─Бtithi leans towards the latter view is indicated by his assertion that what happened was that тАШthe body of Brahm─Б (described in verse 9) now took the form of the Hermaphrodite,тАЩтАФor as he adds later, тАШthe Female form was separated from His own Male form.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШThe said Vir─Бj, having performed austerities,тАЩ produced a person; knowтАФi.e., recogniseтАФthat person to be myself;тАФthere is nothing that is not already known to you, by tradition, which I could describe to you; all that the speaker intends to point out is the purity of his own birth.

The phrase тАШthe creator of this whole worldтАЩ indicates his almighty character. The idea of the speaker is that тАШthe describing of myself as one of excellent birth and superior powers of action will make me more trustworthy.тАЩ

Or, the mention of his own birth might be for the purpose of carrying conviction (removing all doubts); that such may be the sense is shown by the fact that, though the origin of Manu is already known from other sources, yet he himself mentions it; for instance, even though a person is already known from other sources (as the son of a certain person), yet he is askedтАФтАШare you DevadattaтАЩs son?тАЩтАФand he answers тАШyesтАЩ; whereupon certainty of conviction is brought about.

Poets are not ashamed of describing the nobility of their own birth, even though their glories may be already well known.

тАШO best of Br─Бhmaс╣ЗasтАЩтАФis the form of address; тАШbestтАЩ ** means most perfect, most superior.тАФ(33)

тАШBk┼лritejasaс╕е,тАЩ тАШmighty,тАЩ and тАШamitaujasaс╕е,тАЩ тАШpossessing illimitable power,тАЩтАФboth terms mean the same thing; the former with the nominative ending qualifies the creators, and the latter, with the accusative ending, qualifies those created, Manus and the rest.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The various forms of the Yakс╣гa and other beings here mentioned can be known only from the Itih─Бsas and such other sources; they cannot be known by any of the ordinary means of cognition, perception and the rest.тАФThe тАШYakс╣гasтАЩ are the followers of Kuvera;тАФтАШR─Бkс╣гasas,тАЩ Biv─лс╣гaс╣Зa and others;тАФbeings more cruel than these last are тАШPi┼Ы─Бcas,тАЩ who live in unclean places and in deserts, &c., and are inferior to Yakс╣гas and R─Бkс╣гasas; though all three are mischievous; by trickery they draw out the life of living beings, and by some invisible power they bring about diseases: so say persons knowing the Itih─Бsas (stories) and Mantra (Incantations).тАФтАШGandharvas,тАЩ are those followers of the Gods whose chief work consists of singing and dancing;тАФтАШApsarases,тАЩ the courtezans of the Gods, Urva┼Ы─л and the rest;тАФтАШAsuras,тАЩ the GodsтАЩ enemies, Vс╣Ыttra, Virocana, Hiraс╣Зy─Бksa and so forth;тАФтАШN─БgasтАЩ (the Great Serpents), V─Бsuki, Takс╣гaka and the rest;тАФтАШSarpasтАЩ ** (Serpents) are well known;тАФтАШSuparnas,тАЩ the great Birds, Garuс╕Нa and the rest;тАФтАШPitс╣Ыs,тАЩ named тАШSomapa,тАЩ тАШAyyapaтАЩ and so forth, who reside, like Gods, in their own regions; the тАШseveral ordersтАЩ of these also;тАФall these (the mighty sages) called into being.тАФ(37)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШThat kind of action which belongs to the several beings,тАЩтАФi.e., hurtful or harmlessтАФтАШhas been already describedтАЩ;тАФnow тАШI am going to explain the manner of their birth.тАЩ

Objection.тАФ

тАЬWhere has the action been described? In Verses 37 et seq. what occurs is only the mention of the names of several beings, Yakс╣гa, R─Бkс╣гasa and the rest; and their action is not mentioned at all.тАЭ

Our answer is as follows:тАФThe action of each being is indicated by its name; the particular name being acquired by each being by reason of its actions: for instance, the Yakс╣гas are so called because of the act of worshpping, or pervading (тАШYakс╣гaс╣ЗaтАЩ);тАФthe тАШR─Бkс╣гasaтАЩ are so called because of the act of destroying in secret (тАШrahasi kс╣гaс╣ЗanaтАЩ);тАФthe Pi┼Ы─Бchas are so called because of the act of devouring flesh (тАШpi┼Ыit─Б┼ЫanaтАЩ);тАФthe Apsarases are so called because of the act of issuing forth from water (adbhyaс╕е с╣гс╣Ыt─Бс╕е);тАФ the Asuras are so called because of the act of not obtaining sur─Б, in the form of nectar; and so on, the significance of the other names may be traced.

тАШThe manner of their birthтАЩтАФi.e., they are viviparous, oviparous and the like; going to be described in the following verses.тАФ(42)

These are тАШviviparous,тАЩ тАШborn from the Jar─БyuтАЩ; Jar─Бyu is the womb, the place where the f┼Уtus lies; it is in the womb that these beings are conceived first, and it is only when they are emitted from the womb that they become born; this is the manner of the birth of these beings.

рдЙрджреНрднреЗрджрдирдореН рдЙрджреНрднрд┐рддреН ред рднрд╛рд╡реЗ рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН ред рддрддреЛ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдЙрджреНрднрд┐рдЬреНрдЬрд╛рдГ ред рдЙрдкреНрддрдВ рдмреАрдЬрдВ рднреВрдорд┐рдВ рдЪ рднрд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░реНрдп рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдГ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдмреАрдЬрд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рдгреНрдбрд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рдкреНрд░рд░реЛрд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдореВрд▓рд╕реНрдХрдиреНрдзрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рджреГрдвреАрднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрдереНрдФрд╖рдзреНрдпрдГ ред рдУрд╖рдзрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдИрдХрд╛рд░рдГ рдХреГрджрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рджреН рдЗрддрд┐, рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рдЗрджрдВ рддрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд┐рдХрдВ рдХрд░реНрдо ред рдкрд╛рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рдГ рдлрд▓рдкрд╛рдХрдГ рдЕрдиреНрддреЛ рдирд╛рд╢ рдЖрд╕рд╛рдореН рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдкрдХреНрд╡реЗ рдлрд▓реЗ рд╡реНрд░реАрд╣реНрдпрд╛рджрдпреЛ рдирд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐, рдмрд╣реБрдирд╛ рдЪ рдкреБрд╖реНрдкрдлрд▓реЗрдиреЛрдкрдЧрддрд╛рдГ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдФрд╖рдзреАрдирд╛рдВ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдЪ рдпрдерд╛рд╕рдВрднрд╡рдореН рдПрддрджреН рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдгрдореН рее рез.рекрем рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШUdbhidтАЩ stands for тАШudbhedana,тАЩ the act of splitting; the тАШkvipтАЩ affix having a nominal force;тАФтАШthose that are duced by splitting are тАШudbhijjaтАЩ; they are so called because they come into existence by splitting the seed and breaking through the soil; and these are plants; all these plants тАШgrown out of seeds and slipsтАЩ and become fixed in their places by means of roots and trunks and other such things.

тАШOс╣гadhyaс╕етАЩтАФthe right form is тАШoс╣гadhayaс╕етАЩ (because the base ends in short i). Or we may take the word as a form of the base with the long ─л; this lengthening of the vowel being explained, either as according to the V─Бrtika on P─Бс╣Зini 4.1.45, or as a Vedic anomily.

The natural characteristic feature of these oс╣гadhisтАФi.e., AnnualsтАФis as follows: тАШThey with the ripening of their fruitтАЩ;тАФi.e, the ripening of the fruit constitutes their end or perishing; as a matter of fact, the paddy and other such plants perish as soon as their fruit has ripened. They also abound in, are endowed with, many fruits and flowers.

What is stated in this verse is the distinguishing characteristic of oс╣гadhis (Annual plants), and what follows in the following verse, constitutes the distinguishing feature of Vс╣Ыkс╣гas (Perennial Trees); the characters mentioned being attributed to them in accordance with actual facts.тАФ(40)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Medh─Бtithi takes тАШudbhijj─Бс╕е sth─Бvar─Бс╕етАЩ as the subject, and тАШb─лjak─Бс╣Зс╕Нaprarohiс╣Зaс╕етАЩ as the predicate of the sentence. Buhler reverses this.

рдирд┐рдзрд╛рдп рд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрд╛рдкрдпреЗрддрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдПрддрджреН рдЕрдиреВрджреНрдпрддреЗ “рддрдорд╕рд╛ рдмрд╣реБрд░реВрдкреЗрдг” (рдореНрдзреН рез.рекреп) рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрддреН рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдпрд┐рддреБрдореН рее рез.рекрен рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

[The ordinary meaning of the verse is as follows]тАФThose trees, in whom fruits are produced without flowers, are called тАШVanasputi,тАЩ not тАШVс╣Ыkс╣гaтАЩ; while those that bear flowers as well as fruits are, by reason of the presence of both, called тАШVс╣Ыkс╣гaтАЩ As a matter of fact, however, Vanaspatis are also called тАШVс╣Ыkс╣гa,тАЩ and Vс╣Ыkс╣гas are spoken of as тАШVanaspati.тАЩ The particular grounds of such usage will have to be shown later on.

What we hold however (as to the real meaning of this verse), is as follows:тАФThe present work does not make it its business to lay down the meanings of words, in the manner of grammatical works; so that the meaning of the verse cannot be that тАШthose that have such and such a character are denoted by the word Vanaspati, and so forth.тАЩ In fact what is described here is the manner of the birth of fruits; this (manner of birth) having been put forward (in Verse 42) as the subject ih hand. The meaning thus is as follows:тАФFruits are produced in two ways: they are produced without flowers, and also from flowers; and flowers are produced from trees (called Vс╣Ыkс╣гa). Thus then, it follows that, even though the statement is apparently in the form ’those that bear fruits without flowers are to be known as Vanaspati,тАЩтАФyet in view of what forms the subject-matter of the context, the тАШyatтАЩ (тАШwhichтАЩ) and тАШtatтАЩ (тАШthatтАЩ) should be made to change their places; the construction beingтАФтАШthose trees that are known by the name Vanaspati have no flowers, and yet they bear fruitsтАЩ;тАФi.e., in these trees fruits grow without flowers; this construction is adopted on the strength of actual facts. Such altering of the construction on the strength of facts we also find in such cases as the following Though the actual words are in the form тАШv─Бsas─Б pariveс╣гс╣нayeс╣н,тАЩ тАШthe post should bo surrounded with cloth,тАЩтАФyet in as much as the cloth has got to be worn by the man, the words are constructed as тАШstambhe nidh─Бya v─Бsaс╕е paridh─БpayetтАЩ тАШthe cloth should be hung on the post and then made to be worn.тАЩ

Though what is stated in the present verse is a well known fact (and as such did not need to be mentioned in the Smс╣Ыti), yet it has been mentioned with the purpose of serving as an introduction to what is going to be stated below in Verse 49тАФтАШEnveloped in darkness, &c. &c.тАЩтАФ(47)

рдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрд╣рддрд╛ рднреВрдореЗрд░реН рдмрджреНрдзрд╛ рдПрдХрдореВрд▓рд╛ рдЕрдиреЗрдХрдореВрд▓рд╛рд╢реН рдЪ рд▓рддрд╛ рдЙрддреНрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрд┐ рди рдЪ рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдВ рдорд╣рддреАрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдШрд╛рддреЛ рдЧреБрдЪреНрдЫрдЧреБрд▓реНрдорд╢рдмреНрджрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпрдГ рддреГрдгрдореВрд▓рдХрд╛рджрд┐рдГ ред рддрдпреЛрд╕реН рддреБ рднреЗрджрдГ рдкреБрд╖реНрдкрд╡рджреН рдЕрдкреБрд╖реНрдкрдХреГрддреЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рддреГрдгрдЬрд╛рддрдпрдГ рдХреБрд╢рд╢рд╛рджреНрд╡рд▓рд╢рдЩреНрдЦрдкреБрд╖реНрдкреАрдкреНрд░рднреГрддрдпрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдирд╛ рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛ рднреВрдорд┐рдЧрддрд╛рд╕реН рддреГрдгрдкреНрд░рд░реЛрд╣рд╛рдГ ред рд╡рд▓реНрд▓реНрдпреЛ рд╡реНрд░рддрддреНрдпрдГ рднреВрдореЗрд░реН рдЙрддреНрдкрддреНрдп рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рдореН рдЕрдиреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдХрдВрдЪрд┐рддреН рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреЛрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдореН рдЖрд░реБрд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореН рдПрддрддреН рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╡рддреН рдмреАрдЬрдХрд╛рдгреНрдбрд░реБрд╣рдореН рее рез.рекрео рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШClumps and ThicketsтАЩтАФis the name given to the cluster of those shoots that grow together in large numbers, having one or several roots, and do not attain any considerable height; e.g., Copses and the like. Or тАШgucchaтАЩ тАШClumpтАЩ and тАШgulmaтАЩ тАШthicketтАЩ may be taken as two different things; the difference between the two being that, while one bears flowers, the other is flowerless.тАФOther тАШspecies of grassтАФe. g., ku┼Ыa, ┼Ы─Бdbala, ┼Ыaс╣Еkhapuс╣гp─л and so forth.тАФLowspreading tendrilsтАФthe long shoots of grass spreading on the ground.тАФтАШCreepersтАЩтАФare those shoots that grow out of the earth and clinging round a tree or some other object, rise upwards.тАФAll these, like trees, тАШgrow out of seeds and slipsтАЩтАФ(48)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Burnell represents Medh─Бtithi to explain тАШguccha-gulmaтАЩ as тАШone root and many rootsтАЩ. This is not fair. What Medh─Бtithi says is that the names тАШguccha-gulmaтАЩ are applied to clusters of short-growing creepers which may have one root or several roots.тАЩ Kull┼лka defines тАШgucchaтАЩ as the single shoot springing from the root and having no boughs, and тАШgulmaтАЩ as a clump of shoots coming up from one root According to Medh─Бtithi the difference between the two consists in the fact that while the former has flowers, the latter has none.

рдХрд░реНрдо рдЕрдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдЦреНрдпрдВ рд╣реЗрддреБрд░реН рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрдорд╕рд╕реН рддреЗрди рд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рддрд╛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдГ ред рдмрд╣реБрд░реВрдкреЗрдг рд╡рд┐рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рдиреБрднрд╡рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗрди ред рдпрджреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рдЧреБрдгрдВ рддрдерд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рддрдо рдЙрджреНрд░рд┐рдХреНрддрдореН, рдЕрдкрдЪрд┐рддреЗ рд╕рддреНрддреНрд╡рд░рдЬрд╕реА ред рдЕрддрд╕реН рддрдореЛрдмрд╛рд╣реБрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджрджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рдЕрдзрд░реНрдордлрд▓рдореН рдЕрдиреБрднрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реБрдЪрд┐рд░рдореН рдЖрд╕реНрддреЗ ред рд╕рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рддрддреНрд░ рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреН рдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдЦрд▓реЗрд╢рдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рднреБрдЮреНрдЬрддреЗ ред рддрджреН рдЖрд╣- рд╕реБрдЦрджреБрдГрдЦрд╕рдордиреНрд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдиреНрддрдГрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮреЗрддрд┐74 ред рд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛75 рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рд╕реН рддрд▓реНрд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧрд╕реНрдп рдмрд╣рд┐рд░реНрд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рджреЗрдГ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЪреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реВрдкрд╕реНрдпрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреН рдЕрдиреНрддрдГрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрдерд╛рдиреНрддрд░реН рдПрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╢реН рдЪреЗрддрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдХрдгреНрдЯрдХрд╛рджрд┐рддреЛрджрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдХреН рдЪреЗрддрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдиреИрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рд╡рд░рд╛рдГ ред рддреЗ рд╣рд┐ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рддреЛрджрдВ рдкрд░рд╢реБрд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рджрд┐рджреБрдЦрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреЗ ред рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдкрдорджрдореВрд░реНрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдЧрддрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирдГ рее рез.рекреп рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

They are тАШinvested,тАЩ pervaded over, by that тАШDarknessтАЩ (Inertia) of which the cause is тАШaction,тАЩ in the form of vice;тАФтАШmanifold,тАЩ being the cause of the experiencing of various kinds of pain. As a matter of fact, all things are made up of three Constituent Attributes; so what is meant is that in the beings here described the Attribute of тАШDarknessтАЩ is in excess, and those of тАШHarmonyтАЩ and тАШEnergyтАЩ are present in less degrees; hence as abounding in тАШDarknessтАЩ (Inertia), and beset with pain and humiliation, they continue, for a long time, to experience the results of their vicious acts.

In as much as the Attribute of тАШGoodnessтАЩ (Harmony) also is present in them, they do enjoy, in certain conditions, small measures of pleasure also; it is in view of this that they are described as тАШaffected by pleasure and pain.тАЩ

тАШPossessing inner consciousness,тАЩтАФthe term тАШsaс╣Гj├▒─БтАЩ stands for Buddhi, Intelligence (Consciousness); and in as much as activity in the form of going out, speaking and the like,тАФwhich are the effects indicative of the presence of consciousness,тАФis absent (in Trees), they are described as тАШpossessing inner consciousness.тАЩ This must be the meaning of the epithet тАШinnerтАЩ; as otherwise, since every person exercises consciousness only within himself [there would be no point in the epithet at all]. Or, the meaning may be that plants are unable to have any cognisance of the prickings of thorns and other small things, to the extent that human beings are; in fact for the experiencing of pain they stand in need of such massive strokes as cutting with the axe and the like;тАФbeing, in this respect, like animate beings in the state of sleep, intoxication or swoon. [Which shows that plants have their consciousness lying far deeper within than in animals.]тАФ(49)

  • рднреВрддрд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ рднреВрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ рдЬрдиреНрдордорд░рдгрдкреНрд░рдмрдиреНрдзреЗ рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдЧрдордиреЗ ред рдШреЛрд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рджрд╛рд▓рд╕реНрдпрд╡рддрд╛рдВ рднреАрд╖рдгреЗ, рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╡рд┐рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдпреЛрдЧреЛрддреНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛ ред рд╕рддрддрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдХрд╛рд▓рдВ рдЧрдордирд╢рд╛рд▓рд┐рдирд┐77 рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рд┐рдиреНрдпреН рдЕрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдШреЛрд░реЗ рди рдХрджрд╛рдЪрд┐рджреН рдЕрдШреЛрд░реЗ ред рджреЗрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдЧрддрд┐рд╖реНрд╡реН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╕реБрдЪрд┐рд░рдВ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдорд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдШреЛрд░рдГ ред рддрджреН рдЕрдиреЗрди рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдзрд░реНрдордирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╕рдВрд╡рд░реНрдгрдиреЗрди рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдорд╣рд╛рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЬрдирддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрджрд┐рддрд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рджреН рдзрд┐ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдзрд░реНрдордпреЛрд░реН рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдХрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдзреЗрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее рез.релреж рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШEnding with those just mentionedтАЩ;тАФthose conditions of life of which the end, or last, is the condition of the Creeper.тАФтАШConditionтАЩтАФstands for the connection of the soul with a particular body for the experiencing of the result of past acts; and there is no worseтАФi.e., more painful,тАФтАШconditionтАЩ of life than that of Plants; and than the condition of тАШBrahm─БтАЩ there is none higher or superiorтАФi.e., more full of bliss. These тАШconditionsтАЩ are attained by means of good and had acts, respectively called тАШVirtueтАЩ and тАШViceтАЩ; as regards the attaining of the Supreme Brahman, which consists in Salvation, and is in the form of pure bliss,тАФthis proceeds either from pure Knowledge, or from a combination of Knowledge and Action; this we shall describe later on (in Discourse XII).

тАШIn this cycle of births and deaths of created beings;тАЩтАФin this тАШsams─Бra,тАЩ cycle, series of births and deaths, of тАШcreated beings,тАЩ conscious entities; i. e., in which (ordinarily) the entity is not born in a genus other than in which it was in the previous existence;тАФтАШfrightful,тАЩтАФfull of fear, for those that are careless and lazy; it is тАШfull of fearтАЩ in the sense that there is losing of the desirable and coming by the undesirable;тАФтАШconstantly,тАЩ at all times,тАФтАШfluctuating,тАЩ i.e., liable to go off, destructible, (hence) devoid of essence;тАФit is тАШever frightful,тАЩ i.e., it is never not- frightful; it is spoken of as тАШever frightfulтАЩ because even when one has attained the condition of gods, and remains there for a long time, he has to return to death.

This description of the cycle of births and deaths as being due to Virtue and Vice serves to show that Scripture serves an all-important purpose; it has to be born in mind that it is only from Scripture that we can obtain a knowledge of the distinction between тАШVirtueтАЩ and тАШVice.тАЩтАФ(50)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШBh┼лtaтАЩтАФhere stands for the Kс╣гetraj├▒a, the Conscious Being ensouling the bodyтАФaccording to Govindar─Бja and Kull┼лka.

тАШNityamтАЩтАФqualifies тАШghoreтАЩ; тАШEver terribleтАЩ according to Medh─Бtithi, Govindar─Бja and N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa, the last, along with Nandana, however, suggests the reading тАШnityeтАЩ meaning тАШin this eternal sams─Бra.тАЩ

Thus repeatedly suppressing time (of dissolution) by time (of creation and maintenance), he, of inconceivable power, created all this and also myself; [he directed me to maintain it] and then disappeared within himself.тАФ(51)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШThusтАЩтАФi.e., something directly himself, and some under Praj─БpatiтАЩs directions, the Blessed Lord,тАФhaving created produced,тАФall this world,тАФand having directed to maintain (keep going) this world;тАФтАШHeтАЩ whose тАШpower,тАЩ sovereignty over all things, is тАШinconceivable,тАЩ amazingly great, the Creator,тАФтАШdisappeared,тАЩтАФbrought about his own absorption i.e., having renounced the body that he had, of his own will, taken up, He again became unmanifest;тАФтАШwithin himself;тАФ other things become absorbed in the Root Evolvent; but He did not become absorbed in any thing else, He disappeared within his own self; He has no other source wherein He could, like other things, become absorbed; for the simple reason that all beings have their source in Him. Or тАШdisappearingтАЩ may mean desisting from the entire worldly process.

тАШRepeatedly suppressing time by timeтАЩтАФthe Present-participle (тАШsuppressingтАЩ) is connected with the verb тАШhaving oreatedтАЩ; the meaning beingтАФтАШdestroying the time of dissolution by the time of creation and maintenanceтАЩ;тАФтАШagain and again; it will lie described later on that тАШthere are endless creations and dissolutions.тАЩтАФ(61)

B├╝hler

051 When he whose power is incomprehensible, had thus produced the universe and men, he disappeared in himself, repeatedly suppressing one period by means of the other.
